–ê —á—Ç–æ —Ç—ã —Å–¥–µ–ª–∞–ª –¥–ª—è –∫–æ—Ç—ç!?
Sistema held a presentation for bond investors in Moscow yesterday (3 October), hosted by CFO Vladimir Travkov. The event was centred on the upcoming put option Sistema is facing on its RUB 5bn bond (1P01 series) on 9 October. The company did not provide many new details to its earlier-declared deleveraging plans, though it did affirm that they remain the key priority. According to management, the issuer plans to repay its Eurobond (AFKSRU 19) partially using its accumulated liquidity and through new local borrowing. With this note, we share our key takeaways from the meeting.
Target to decrease debt load to RUB 150bn affirmed, but it could take longer. Upon reporting its 2Q18 IFRS results in August, Sistema announced plans to decrease its debt at the corporate centre level from RUB 237bn at the end of 1H18 toward RUB 160-190bn (~USD 2.4-2.9bn currently) by YE18, and below RUB 150bn by the end of 2Q19. Based on the management comments we heard yesterday, the RUB 150bn debt target is still in place, but the timeline for it is now more flexible (until YE19). Still, the company sounded as if it was focused on delivering on the guidance, and also made it clear that deleveraging is currently being prioritised over shareholder distributions.
Deleveraging progress largely depends on asset sale. As noted by management, via its expected dividend inflow, Sistema is likely to be able to decrease its debt load by RUB 10-15bn annually, meaning that the actual deleveraging speed largely depends on the company‚Äôs asset monetisation either through attracting strategic investors or IPOs. At the same time, management noted that in the current market conditions, IPOs look unlikely; no specific assets were named as being close to being sold in any form. In our view, Detskiy Mir remains the main asset for potential sale, which could help Sistema achieve its declared deleveraging target. In September, Sistema‚Äôs controlling shareholder, Vladimir Evtushenkov, was quoted by Interfax as saying that there are 12 potential buyers interested in the asset, so we feel that Sistema‚Äôs valuation of Detskiy Mir is aggressive, and that the company is not rushing to close the deal. In terms of the possible sale of Sistema‚Äôs remaining 43.24% shares in MTS Bank to MTS (Ba1/BB/BB+), the transaction is on hold, with no decision yet made (we previously estimated it could bring some RUB 20bn (prior to tax) cash inflow for Sistema).
New offered RUB bond coupon of 9.75% looks just fair. Sistema is offering the holders of its 1P01 series a RUB bond to extend the maturity until March 2022 (3.5 years) at a coupon rate of 9.75%. The new maturity was chosen based on its comfortable fit to the issuer‚Äôs current debt repayment schedule. To us, the new coupon rate looks just fair: Sistema currently has an outstanding bond (1P06 series) of comparable duration yielding about the same. On the other hand, the offer is not generous compared with alternative options we now see in the RUB bond market among B/BB-rated corporates. Moreover, the new possible issuance of RUB bonds from Sistema over the next 12 months might pressure its existing curve, in our view (in 2019, Sistema‚Äôs debt repayments are seeing their local peak of RUB 60.7bn). As noted by management, Sistema‚Äôs Eurobond maturity in May could be partially financed via a new RUB bond placement. It is also worth keeping in mind that in February next year, Sistema faces a put option on another bond (1P07 series) of RUB 10bn notional, which it will also likely try to extend, in our view. Currently, Sistema has a total of RUB 61.5bn in RUB bonds outstanding (26% of its total debt at the corporate centre level).
